The Relationship Between Psychic and Verbal Speech
Dardeer distinguishes psychic from verbal speech and discusses the implications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between psychic and verbal speech, and how the heavenly books and prophetic revelation relate to the eternal attribute.

Core Idea
Verbal speech points to psychic speech, which alone is eternal.

After defining divine speech as a psychic attribute, Dardeer explains how it relates to the verbal speech we read in scriptures. He clarifies that verbal speech is a proof of the psychic speech, and that the heavenly books communicate only part of its meaning. He also addresses the famous case of Allah's speech to Moses.

Guided Path
1
Read the distinction
Pay attention to the relationship between the two types of speech: verbal speech is daleel (proof) of psychic speech.
The proof is distinct from the proven.
2
Note the division of verbal speech
Verbal speech divides into promise, threat, command, prohibition, and report. Why can't the eternal attribute be divided?
Think about the nature of a simple eternal attribute.
3
Consider the heavenly books
How do they relate to the psychic speech? They indicate some in detail and all in summary.
4
Examine the Moses incident
What does this incident show about the nature of divine speech?
The Ashʿarī position is that it was psychic speech.

Divine Hearing and Sight: Eternal Attributes of Complete Disclosure
Dardeer defines divine hearing and sight as eternal attributes causing complete disclosure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature of divine hearing and sight as eternal attributes that cause full disclosure of existents, distinct from knowledge, and the obligation to affirm them without modality.

Core Idea
Allah's hearing and sight bring complete disclosure, distinct from knowledge.

In this passage, Imam Dardeer explains the sixth and seventh attributes of meanings: hearing and sight. He clarifies that these are eternal attributes that cause a complete disclosure of all existents, and that their mode of disclosure is different from that of knowledge. He then emphasizes the obligation of believing in these attributes without attempting to understand how, because Allah is unlike anything.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how Dardeer defines hearing and sight as eternal attributes that cause complete disclosure.
Pay attention to the phrasing: 'two eternal attributes by which all existents are disclosed with complete disclosure.'
2
Compare disclosure modes
Notice that Dardeer emphasizes that disclosure by hearing and sight differs from disclosure by knowledge, and that each of them differs from the other. This distinction preserves the uniqueness of each attribute.
The disclosure modes are distinct, even though all are complete.
3
Understand the obligation
The passage concludes with the obligation to affirm the attributes without knowing the modality (kayfiyya). Reflect on why this is necessary: because Allah is like nothing.
This is a universal principle for all attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) سادسها (السمعُ) وسابعها (الإبصارُ)، يعني: البصر، فقد أطلَقَ اسْمَ الْمُسَبَّبِ وأراد السبب مجازًا، يدلُّ على مُرادِه أَنَّ الكلام في المعاني، وكذا ما يأتي في التعلق. ولو قال: «ثُمَّ البصر» لكانَ أوضحَ. والسمع والبصرُ صِفَتانِ أزليَّتان ينكشِفُ بهما جميعُ الموجوداتِ انكشاف تاما. والانكشاف بهما يغاير الانكشاف بالعِلْم، كما أنَّ الانكشاف بإحداهما يغاير الانكشاف بالأخرى. ثُمَّ فَرَّعَ عَلَى صِفاتِ المعاني في الجُمْلة، إذ التفريعُ إنما يَظْهَرُ على الأربعةِ الأُوَلِ. الواجب على المكلف اعتقاد ثبوت صفاته تعالى من غير معرفة الكنه على وجه يخالف صفات المخلوقات لأنه تعالى لَيْسَ كَمِثْلِهِ شَيْءٌ ﴾ [الشورى: ١١]
(And) the sixth of them is hearing and the seventh is sight, meaning vision. He used the name of the effect and intended the cause metaphorically, indicating his intent that the discussion is about attributes of meanings, and similarly what comes regarding relational attributes. And if he had said 'then vision' it would be clearer. Hearing and sight are two eternal attributes by which all existents are disclosed with complete disclosure. And the disclosure by them differs from disclosure by knowledge, just as the disclosure by one of them differs from disclosure by the other. Then he branched off from the attributes of meanings in general, for the branching only becomes apparent on the first four. It is obligatory upon the responsible person to believe in the establishment of His attributes, exalted is He, without knowing the modality, in a manner that opposes the attributes of created beings, because He, exalted is He, is like nothing.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage defines the sixth and seventh attributes of meanings: divine hearing (samʿ) and sight (baṣar). The author notes that the poet used the name of the effect (al-musabbab) and intended the cause metaphorically, meaning that when he said 'hearing and sight' he referred to the attributes themselves, not their effects. He then states that these are two eternal attributes that bring about a complete disclosure (inkishāf tāmm) of all existents. This disclosure is distinct from the disclosure by knowledge, and each of them (hearing and sight) has a distinct mode of disclosure. Next, the author makes a general remark: the branching off from the attributes of meanings only becomes apparent with the first four attributes (life, knowledge, will, and power). Finally, he adds a general principle: it is obligatory for every responsible person to affirm the attributes of Allah without attempting to understand their modality (al-kayfiyya), because Allah is unlike anything in creation.

God as the Free Agent: Refuting Necessary Causality
Dardeer refutes the philosophers' claim that God is a necessary cause and proves He is a free agent using the diversity of the world.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the diversity of the world proves that God is a free agent, not a necessary cause, and how this refutes the philosophers' doctrine.

Core Idea
God's free will is proven by the world's diversity.

In this passage, Imam Dardeer refutes the philosophers' claim that God acts by necessity, like a natural or efficient cause. He shows that the variety in creation—animate, inanimate, dark, light, sweet, bitter—cannot come from a single, uniform cause. This leads him to affirm that God is al-Fāʿil al-Mukhtār, the Free Agent, who creates as He wills and is not compelled by any external factor.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Let the author's direct style and Quranic quotations sink in before analyzing.
Notice the strong language against the philosophers.
2
Identify the philosophers' claim and Dardeer's response
The philosophers say God is a 'doer by cause' (فاعل بالعلة). Dardeer refutes this by affirming God as the Free Agent. Find how he contrasts the two views.
3
Examine the evidence from the diversity of the world
The world contains many different kinds: inanimate/living, dark/luminous, sweet/bitter. Dardeer argues this diversity cannot result from a single necessary cause. Reflect on why that is a strong proof.
He quotes the Quran about fruits watered by the same water but differing in taste.
4
Reflect on the consequences and warning
Dardeer states that the philosophers' view leads to denying bodily resurrection and essential divine attributes. He ends with a stern warning about their deceptive arguments.
The passage shows how false beliefs can lead to further errors.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَولُه (فهْوَ الإِلهُ) أي : المعبودُ بحَقِّ، (الفاعل المختارُ) أي: الذي إِنْ شَاءَ فَعَلَ وَإِنْ شاء ترك، وَرَبُّكَ يَخْلُقُ مَا يَشَاءُ وَيَختَارُ، لا أنه فاعل بالطبع أو بالعلة، خلاف للفلاسفة الملعونين، ولذا قالوا بقدَمِ العالم، لأنه يلزَمُ مِنْ قِدَمِ العِلَّةِ قِدَمُ المعلول ونفَوا عَن الله تعالى صفاته الذاتية، وهو مذهَبْ باطلٌ وكُفْرٌ مراح، إلى غير ذلك، كما أشار ومما يدلُّ على بطلانه تنوُّعُ العالم إلى أنواع مختلفة، فبعضه جماد، وبعضُه حيوان وبعضُه ظُلْماني، وبعضُه نوران، وبعضُه حُلْو، وبعضُه له الكِتابُ العزيز في كثير مِنَ الآي. قال تعالى: يُسْقَى بِمَاءِ وَاحِدٍ وَنُفَضِّلُ بَعْضَهَا عَلَى بَعْضٍ فِي الْأُكُل إِنَّ فِي ذَلِكَ لَآيَاتٍ لِّقَوْمٍ يَعْقِلُونَ)، فهذا يشير إلى أنَّ هؤلاء الخاسرين ليسوا بعقلاء، إذْ فِعلُ العِلّة والطبيعة ليس إلا شيئًا واحِدًا غَيْرَ مُختلف أَفَلاَ يَنظُرُونَ إِلَى الإِبْل كَيْفَ خُلِقَتْ وَإِلَى السَّمَاءِ كَيْفَ رُفِعَتْ وَإِلَى الْجِبَالِ كَيْفَ نُصِبَتْ وَإِلَى الْأَرْضَ كَيْفَ سُطِحَتْ ، أَفَلَمْ يَنظُرُوا إِلَى السَّمَاءِ فَوْقَهُمْ كَيْفَ بَنَيْنَاهَا وَزَيَّنَّاهَا وَمَا لَهَا مِن فُرُوج * وَالْأَرْضَ مَدَدْنَاهَا وَأَلْقَيْنَا فِيهَا رَوَاسِيَ وَأَنبَتْنَا فِيهَا مِن كُلِّ زَوْجٍ بَهِيجٍ ولَكِنْ مَنْ يُضْلِ اللَّهُ فما له مِنْ هَادٍ. ومما بنوه على مذهبهم عدَمُ المعاد الجسماني، وقد زخرفوا مذاهبهم بشُبَه ظنّيّةٍ خيالية، كسَراب بقيعة يحسبه الظمآن ماءً حتى إذا جاءه لم يجده شَيئًا، فضلوا وأَضَلُّوا حتى ظَنَّ كثيرٌ مِنَ الناسِ أنَّ هذهِ الزخارفَ عِلْمٌ ، بل فضَّلوا المتمسكين بها على عُلماء الشريعة، كلّا سَوفَ يعلمون، ثُمَّ كَلَّا سَوفَ يعلمون.
His saying (So He is al-Ilah) meaning: the One truly worshipped, (the Free Agent) meaning: He who if He wills He does and if He wills He leaves, and your Lord creates what He wills and chooses. He is not a doer by nature or by cause, contrary to the accursed philosophers, and therefore they said with the pre-eternity of the world, because from the pre-eternity of the cause follows the pre-eternity of the effect, and they denied of Allah, exalted, His essential attributes, and it is a false and blasphemous doctrine, to other things, as he indicated. And among what indicates its falsity is the diversity of the world into different kinds: some of it inanimate, some alive, some dark, some luminous, some sweet, some bitter. The Mighty Book in many verses: He said, exalted: 'Watered with one water, and We make some of them excel others in fruit. Indeed in that are signs for a people who reason.' This indicates that these losers are not intelligent, for the action of cause and nature is only one thing, not diverse. Do they not look at the camels how they are created? And at the sky how it is raised? And at the mountains how they are set up? And at the earth how it is spread out? Have they not looked at the heaven above them, how We built it and adorned it, and it has no fissures? And the earth We spread out, and cast therein firm mountains, and caused to grow therein every beautiful kind? But whoever Allah leaves astray has no guide. And among what they built upon their doctrine is the denial of bodily resurrection. And they adorned their doctrines with speculative imaginary doubts, like a mirage in a desert which the thirsty supposes is water until when he comes to it he finds it nothing. So they went astray and led astray until many people thought that these adornments are knowledge, rather they preferred those who adhered to them over the scholars of Sharia. No! They will know, then no! They will know.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the philosophers' claim that God is a necessary cause (فاعل بالعلة) or a natural cause (فاعل بالطبع). The author begins by explaining the phrase from the original poem: 'فهو الإله' (So He is al-Ilah), defining al-Ilah as the One truly worshipped, and 'الفاعل المختار' (the Free Agent), meaning that God does as He wills—He acts when He wills and refrains when He wills. This is supported by the Quranic verse: 'Your Lord creates what He wills and chooses.' The key point is that God is not a doer by nature or by cause, which is the position of the accursed philosophers. Because they claim that God is a necessary cause, they are forced to assert the pre-eternity of the world (since a necessary cause entails a necessary effect), and they also deny God's essential attributes. The author declares this doctrine false and blasphemous. Then he provides evidence for its falsity: the diversity of the world. The world consists of many different kinds—inanimate, animate, dark, luminous, sweet, bitter—yet they all come from the same water, as the Quran says: 'Watered with one water, and We make some of them excel others in fruit.' This diversity cannot result from a single cause that produces only one effect; it must be from a free agent who chooses to differentiate. Thus those who deny this are not intelligent. The author then cites more Quranic verses calling for reflection on creation. He also mentions that the philosophers' doctrine leads to the denial of bodily resurrection. Finally, he describes how the philosophers have adorned their false doctrines with deceptive, speculative doubts, like a mirage, leading many people astray even to the point of preferring them over scholars of Sharia. The passage ends with a stern warning: 'No! They will know, then no! They will know.'

Key Terms
الفاعل المختار
فاعل بالطبع
فاعل بالعلة
الفلاسفة الملعونون
قدَم العالم
المعاد الجسماني
صفاته الذاتية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God's action is necessitated like natural causation, i.e., He cannot do otherwise.
Correction: God is a free agent; He acts by will and choice, as proven by the diversity of creation.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what evidence does Dardeer present to refute the philosophers' claim that God is a necessary cause?
A) The pre-eternity of the world
B) The diversity of the world
C) The denial of bodily resurrection
D) The philosophers' own statements

Key Takeaway
The diversity of creation proves that God is a free agent who acts by will, not by nature or necessary cause.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you observe the diversity in creation—sweet and bitter, light and dark—do you truly see it as a sign that God is a free agent, or do you unconsciously treat the world as governed by impersonal, necessary laws? In what area of your life today has familiarity dulled your wonder at the Creator's free choice? Decide one specific natural diversity to ponder tonight, and let it lead you to praise Allah for His absolute freedom.
?
The philosophers were led astray by their own speculations, preferring a mirage over the clear signs of the Quran. In your own pursuit of knowledge, have you ever prioritized clever arguments or worldly wisdom over the straightforward guidance of revelation? Where might you be trusting your own reasoning more than the words of Allah? Repent and commit to placing scripture above speculation.
?
The passage warns that many people preferred the philosophers over the scholars of Sharia. Is there any area in your life where you value secular expertise or popular opinion more than the teachings of Islam? How can you realign your priorities so that the truth from the Quran and Sunnah becomes your ultimate authority? List one practical step you will take to honor Islamic scholarship over cultural or academic fads.

Divine Attributes
beginner

The Seven Agreed Attributes and the Exclusion of Perception and Moral Attributes
Dardeer explains his selection of the seven attributes and the exclusion of perception and moral attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Dardeer restricts the divine attributes to seven agreed-upon attributes of meaning and why he omits the attribute of perception and the moral attributes according to Ash'ari theology.

Core Idea
The seven attributes of meaning are core; perception is suspended, and moral attributes are not separate existences.

Dardeer begins by clarifying the scope of his discussion. He limits himself to the seven attributes of meaning that are universally accepted among theologians, setting aside the debated attribute of perception and the moral attributes. This careful delimitation is based on the Ash'ari position that moral attributes are not additional entities but merely expressions of the subsistence of the attributes in the essence. This lesson establishes the foundational set of attributes that require further explanation of their attachment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the seven agreed attributes
Recognize that Dardeer focuses on the seven attributes of meaning (ṣifāt al-maʿānī) that are unanimously accepted among the people (al-qawm).
These are the core divine attributes discussed in kalam.
2
Understand the omission of perception
Dardeer excludes the attribute of perception (al-idrāk) because the correct position is to suspend judgment (tawaqquf) – it is not definitively established.
Some theologians added it, but Dardeer avoids it.
3
Grasp the Ash'ari position on moral attributes
The moral attributes (al-ṣifāt al-maʿnawiyya) like being Knowing, Living, Powerful are not additional realities. They are merely expressions of the subsistence of the attributes of meaning in the essence.
This is based on the rejection of the concept of 'mode' (ḥāl) and the principle that there is no intermediary between existence and non-existence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان تعلقات صفات المعاني واعْلَمُ أنَّ هذه الصفات السبعَ هي المتَّفَقُ عليها بَينَ القوم، فلذا اقتصرت عليها ولم أَزِدْ ما زادَ بعضُهم مِنْ صِفةِ الإِدْراكِ، ولأنَّ الحقِّ فيها الوقْفُ، ولم أذكُرِ الصَّفات المعنوية الملازمة للسبع المعاني، وهي كونه تعالى عالما، وكُونُه حَيَّا، وكُونُه تعالى قادرًا. إلخ؛ لأنَّ الحقِّ ما ذهب إليه إمامنا إمام أهل السُّنّة أبو الحسن الأشعري رَضِيَ اللهُ مِنْ أنها ليست بزائدة على المعاني، بل هي عبارةً عنْ قيام المعاني بالذات، لا أَنَّ هَا ثُبوتا في الخارج عن الذهنِ؛ بناءً على نفي الحال، وأنه لا واسطة بين الموجود والمعدوم. ۳۷ - وواجب تعليقُ ذي الصَّفات * حتّاً دَوامًا ما عدا الحياة ولما فرَغَ مِنْ بيانِ صِفاتِ المعاني شرَعَ في بيان تعلّقها، والتعَلَّقُ: اقتضاءُ الصفة أمرًا زائدا على قيامها بالذات، كاقتضاء العِلم معلوما ينكشِفُ به، واقتضاء الإرادة مرادًا يتخصَّصُ بها، واقتضاء القُدْرة مقدورًا، وهكذا. فقال: (وواجب) عقلا (تعليق (ذي) أي: هذه الصفات) أي: صفات المعاني (حتم) أي: لزوما ، (دَواما) أي: على سبيل الدوام والاستمرار، وهذا مِنْ زيادةِ التأكيد؛ لأنَّ الواجب النقلي شأنه ذلك، ما عدا الحياة) بالجر، ف«ما» زائدةٌ، و«عدا» حرفُ جَر، فيجب على كُلِّ مُكَلَّف أنْ يعتقد ذلك. وحاصله : أنَّ هذه الصفاتِ بالنِّسبةِ للتَّعَلُّقِ وعَدَمِه أربعة أقسام :
Explanation of the attachments of the attributes of meaning. And know that these seven attributes are those agreed upon among the people, so I limited myself to them and did not add what some added of the attribute of perception, because the truth regarding it is suspension. And I did not mention the moral attributes concomitant to the seven attributes of meaning, such as His being Exalted as Knowing, His being Living, His being Exalted as Powerful, etc., because the truth is what our Imam, the Imam of the Ahl al-Sunnah, Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, may Allah be pleased with him, went to: that they are not additional to the attributes of meaning, but rather they are an expression of the subsisting of the attributes in the essence, not that they have a separate existence in the external world; this is based on the negation of modes (ḥāl) and that there is no intermediary between existent and non-existent. 37 - And necessary is the attachment of these attributes * eternally perpetually except life. When he finished explaining the attributes of meaning, he proceeded to explain their attachment. And 'attachment' (taʿalluq) is: the attribute requiring something additional to its subsistence in the essence, such as knowledge requiring a known object that is disclosed by it, and will requiring an object willed that becomes particularized by it, and power requiring an object of power, and so on. So he said: 'And necessary' rationally 'attachment of these' i.e. these attributes, i.e. the attributes of meaning, 'eternally' i.e. perpetually, 'perpetually' i.e. on the way of perpetuity and continuance, and this is for increased emphasis, because what is necessary by transmission is of that nature, 'except life' – with genitive, with 'mā' being extra and 'ʿadā' a preposition. So it is obligatory for every responsible person to believe that. And its summary: these attributes, with respect to having attachment or not, are of four categories: ...
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the attributes of meaning (ṣifāt al-maʿānī) and their necessary attachment (taʿalluq). Dardeer first notes that the seven attributes of meaning are those agreed upon by the theological community; he restricts himself to them and does not include the attribute of perception (al-idrāk) added by some, because the correct position is to suspend judgment on it. He also omits the moral attributes (al-ṣifāt al-maʿnawiyya) – like His being Knowing, Living, Powerful – which are concomitant to the seven attributes of meaning, because according to Imam al-Ashʿarī they are not additional realities but merely expressions of the subsistence of the attributes in the essence; there is no separate existence for them in the external world, based on the rejection of the concept of 'mode' (ḥāl) and the principle that there is no intermediary between existence and non-existence. Then he proceeds to explain the attachment of these attributes. Attachment is defined as the attribute's requirement of something additional to its subsistence in the essence: e.g., knowledge requires a known object, will requires an object willed, power requires an object of power, etc. He then comments on the line from the poem: 'And necessary is the attachment of these attributes * eternally perpetually except life.' The necessity is rational (ʿaqlan). 'Eternally' and 'perpetually' emphasize that the attachment is continuous and unceasing. 'Except life' – life is excluded because it does not attach to any object; it is a self-subsistent attribute. The final sentence summarizes that these attributes, regarding whether they have attachment or not, fall into four categories (which are probably elaborated in the following text not included here).

Key Terms
الصفات السبع
صفات المعاني
الإدراك
الصفات المعنوية
الحال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the moral attributes (like Being Knowing) are separate entities from the attributes of meaning.
Correction: According to Ash'ari, they are not additional but merely express the subsistence of the attributes in the essence.

Checkpoint
Why does Dardeer exclude the attribute of perception (al-idrāk) from his discussion?
A) Because it is not agreed upon among theologians.
B) Because the truth about it is suspended (tawaqquf).
C) Because it is not an attribute of meaning.
D) Because it is included in the moral attributes.

Key Takeaway
The seven attributes of meaning are foundational; perception is suspended, and moral attributes are not independent entities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a matter of faith that scholars have suspended judgment on, like the attribute of perception, do you feel compelled to have a definitive answer, or can you trust the humility of tawaqquf? What does that reveal about your need for certainty?
?
You affirm that Allah is Knowing, Living, Powerful—but do you treat these as mere titles or as realities that should transform how you live? Are you content with knowing about them, or do you actually seek to let them shape your awe and dependence?
?
The Ash'ari position says moral attributes are not separate entities but the very subsistence of attributes in the essence. Do you live as though your knowledge of Allah is a separate 'fact' or as something that subsists in your very being, changing how you see everything?

The Necessary Attachment of Attributes and the Exception of Life
Dardeer defines ta'alluq and explains the necessity of attachment except for life.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the concept of ta'alluq (attachment) for the attributes of meaning and why life is excluded from this necessity.

Core Idea
Ta'alluq is the attribute's requirement of an object; life uniquely lacks this attachment.

After establishing the seven attributes, Dardeer explains their attachment (taʿalluq). He defines attachment as the attribute's requirement of an additional object beyond its subsistence in the essence. Knowledge requires a known, will a willed object, power a power object, etc. However, the attribute of life is an exception — it does not attach to any object. This lesson explains the rational necessity of this attachment and its perpetual nature.

Guided Path
1
Define ta'alluq
Understand that ta'alluq is the attribute's requirement of something additional to its subsistence in the essence. It is not part of the attribute itself but a logical relation.
For example, knowledge cannot be conceived without a known object.
2
Examine the examples
Dardeer provides examples: knowledge requires a known, will requires a willed object, power requires an object of power. Each attribute has a specific relation.
3
Study the poetic line
The line 'And necessary is the attachment of these attributes * eternally perpetually except life' summarizes the rule: attachment is rationally necessary and perpetual, except for life.
The repetition 'eternally perpetually' emphasizes continuity.
4
Understand the exception of life
Life is excluded because it does not require an object; it is self-subsistent. This is a key distinction among the attributes of meaning.
The four categories of attributes regarding attachment are alluded to but not detailed here.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان تعلقات صفات المعاني واعْلَمُ أنَّ هذه الصفات السبعَ هي المتَّفَقُ عليها بَينَ القوم، فلذا اقتصرت عليها ولم أَزِدْ ما زادَ بعضُهم مِنْ صِفةِ الإِدْراكِ، ولأنَّ الحقِّ فيها الوقْفُ، ولم أذكُرِ الصَّفات المعنوية الملازمة للسبع المعاني، وهي كونه تعالى عالما، وكُونُه حَيَّا، وكُونُه تعالى قادرًا. إلخ؛ لأنَّ الحقِّ ما ذهب إليه إمامنا إمام أهل السُّنّة أبو الحسن الأشعري رَضِيَ اللهُ مِنْ أنها ليست بزائدة على المعاني، بل هي عبارةً عنْ قيام المعاني بالذات، لا أَنَّ هَا ثُبوتا في الخارج عن الذهنِ؛ بناءً على نفي الحال، وأنه لا واسطة بين الموجود والمعدوم. ۳۷ - وواجب تعليقُ ذي الصَّفات * حتّاً دَوامًا ما عدا الحياة ولما فرَغَ مِنْ بيانِ صِفاتِ المعاني شرَعَ في بيان تعلّقها، والتعَلَّقُ: اقتضاءُ الصفة أمرًا زائدا على قيامها بالذات، كاقتضاء العِلم معلوما ينكشِفُ به، واقتضاء الإرادة مرادًا يتخصَّصُ بها، واقتضاء القُدْرة مقدورًا، وهكذا. فقال: (وواجب) عقلا (تعليق (ذي) أي: هذه الصفات) أي: صفات المعاني (حتم) أي: لزوما ، (دَواما) أي: على سبيل الدوام والاستمرار، وهذا مِنْ زيادةِ التأكيد؛ لأنَّ الواجب النقلي شأنه ذلك، ما عدا الحياة) بالجر، ف«ما» زائدةٌ، و«عدا» حرفُ جَر، فيجب على كُلِّ مُكَلَّف أنْ يعتقد ذلك. وحاصله : أنَّ هذه الصفاتِ بالنِّسبةِ للتَّعَلُّقِ وعَدَمِه أربعة أقسام :

Attachment is defined as the attribute's requirement of something additional to its subsistence in the essence: e.g., knowledge requires a known object, will requires an object willed, power requires an object of power, etc. He then comments on the line from the poem: 'And necessary is the attachment of these attributes * eternally perpetually except life.' The necessity is rational (ʿaqlan). 'Eternally' and 'perpetually' emphasize that the attachment is continuous and unceasing. 'Except life' – life is excluded because it does not attach to any object; it is a self-subsistent attribute. The final sentence summarizes that these attributes, regarding whether they have attachment or not, fall into four categories (which are probably elaborated in the following text not included here).

الحياة
التعليق
الواجب

Misconception: One might think that the attribute of life also has an attachment, like requiring a living being.
Correction: Life is self-subsistent and does not attach to any object; it is the only attribute of meaning without ta'alluq.

Checkpoint

A) The seven attributes of meaning
B) The necessity of attachment
C) The moral attributes agreed upon

Key Takeaway

?

Consider that Allah's knowledge is attached to you as a known object. Are you living as though your every action is fully disclosed to Him? What would change if you truly believed that?
?
The exception of life reminds you that Allah's essence is not constrained by relations. Which created relationships (e.g., with people, possessions) have you falsely elevated to the status of necessities for your well-being? How will you break their hold on your heart?

The Seven Agreed Attributes and Omission of Perception
Author explains restriction to seven attributes and omission of perception and modal attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the author restricts the list of divine attributes to seven, why he omits perception, and why he does not include modal attributes.

Core Idea
The author only lists attributes on which there is agreement, and he avoids speculative additions.

In this passage, the author clarifies his selection of divine attributes. He explains that he only lists the seven that are unanimously agreed upon among theologians. He also addresses why he excludes the attribute of perception and why he does not mention the so-called modal attributes, following the Ash'ari position. Let's read his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once to get the overall argument.
Pay attention to the author's three decisions.
2
Identify the three decisions
Notice that the author makes three choices: 1) listing only the seven agreed attributes, 2) omitting perception, 3) omitting modal attributes.
3
Understand the reasoning
The author gives reasons for each: agreement, suspension of judgment on perception, and the Ash'ari view that modal attributes are not separate entities.
Focus on the concept of 'waqf' (suspension).
4
Reflect on the concept of 'waqf' and modal attributes
Consider why suspending judgment on perception might be the correct position. Also understand the Ash'ari position that modal attributes are not extra entities.
This connects to the broader principle of avoiding unnecessary affirmations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن هذه الصفات السبع هي المتفق عليها بين القوم، فلذا اقتصرت عليها ولم أزد ما زاد بعضهم من صفة الإدراك، ولأن الحق فيها الوقف، ولم أذكر الصفات المعنوية الملازمة للسبع المعاني، وهي كونه تعالى عالما، وكونه حيا، وكونه تعالى قادرا. إلخ؛ لأن الحق ما ذهب إليه إمامنا إمام أهل السنة أبو الحسن الأشعري رضي الله عنه من أنها ليست بزائدة على المعاني، بل هي عبارة عن قيام المعاني بالذات، لا أن لها ثبوتا في الخارج عن الذهن؛ بناء على نفي الحال، وأنه لا واسطة بين الموجود والمعدوم.
Know that these seven attributes are agreed upon among the people (the theologians), so I restricted myself to them and did not add what some added of the attribute of perception (al-idrāk), because the truth regarding it is suspension (al-waqf). And I did not mention the modal attributes (al-ṣifāt al-ma‘nawiyya) that are inseparable from the seven attributes of meaning (al-ma‘ānī), namely that He is knowing, that He is living, and that He is powerful, etc.; because the truth is what our imam, the imam of the Ahl al-Sunna, Abu al-Hasan al-Ash‘ari (may Allah be pleased with him) held: that they are not additional to the meanings (al-ma‘ānī), but rather they are an expression of the subsistence of the meanings in the essence, not that they have existence in the external world, based on the denial of the state (al-ḥāl), and that there is no intermediate between existent and non-existent.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage is a clarification regarding the selection of attributes discussed. The author explains why he only lists seven attributes: because these are unanimously accepted. He refrains from including the attribute of perception (al-idrāk), which some theologians added, because the correct position is to suspend judgment on it. He also explains why he does not mention the so-called 'modal attributes' (al-ṣifāt al-ma‘nawiyya) such as being knowing, living, powerful, etc. The reason is that, according to Imam al-Ash‘ari, these are not actually distinct eternal attributes; they are merely the fact that the attribute of meaning (e.g., knowledge) subsists in the essence. They have no extra mental existence. This is based on the rejection of the 'state' (al-ḥāl) as an intermediate between existence and non-existence.

Key Terms
الصفات السبع
الإدراك
الصفات المعنوية
الحال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the modal attributes (like being knowing) are additional eternal attributes separate from the attributes of meaning.
Correction: According to the Ash'ari position, they are not additional; they are expressions of the existence of the meanings in the essence, with no extra existence in the external world.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The author's selection of divine attributes is based on consensus and cautious theological method, avoiding speculative additions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The modal attributes are not additional to the meanings; they are expressions of their subsistence in the essence. Do you ever treat descriptions of Allah as separate entities, forgetting that they are simply ways of speaking about His reality? How can you ensure your heart remains focused on the oneness of His essence rather than multiplying concepts?
?
The Ash'ari position denies any intermediate between existent and non-existent. How does this affect your understanding of Allah's attributes? Are you comfortable with the idea that some theological questions are left unsettled, or do you hunger for certainty even where scholars have paused?

The Attachment of Divine Attributes: Definition and Classification
Author defines attachment and classifies attributes into four categories regarding it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand what 'attachment' (ta'alluq) means for the divine attributes of meaning, and how these attributes are classified into four categories based on their attachment.

Core Idea
Attachment is not separation—it means an attribute requires an object.

In this passage, Imam al-Dardir builds on the discussion of the attributes of meaning (ṣifāt al-ma‘ānī) by explaining how each attribute relates to its object. This concept of 'attachment' is crucial for understanding the scope of each attribute. The author defines the term and then gives a concise classification into four types, which the commentary unpacks.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage once to get a feel for the author's style. Then read the literal translation to understand the meaning.
Notice the technical term 'ta'alluq' and its definition.
2
Identify the definition of ta'alluq
The passage defines attachment as an attribute requiring an extra thing beyond its subsistence in the essence. Understand that this is not physical attachment but logical dependency.
Examples: knowledge requires an object known.
3
Understand the ruling: intellectually obligatory
The author states that it is intellectually obligatory for these attributes to have attachment perpetually, except for life. This is a key theological point.
The exception of life is important.
4
Map the four categories of attributes
The classification: (1) Life: no attachment. (2) Knowledge and Speech: attach to all rational judgments. (3) Other attributes: will attaches to possibles only, power to all existents? The passage ends with a verse.
Use the commentary to see the subcategories clearly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولما فرغ من بيان صفات المعاني شرع في بيان تعلقها، والتعلق: اقتضاء الصفة أمرا زائدا على قيامها بالذات، كاقتضاء العلم معلوما ينكشف به، واقتضاء الإرادة مرادا يتخصص بها، واقتضاء القدرة مقدورا، وهكذا. فقال: (وواجب) عقلا (تعليق ذي) أي: هذه الصفات (أي: صفات المعاني) (حتم) أي: لزوما، (دواما) أي: على سبيل الدوام والاستمرار، وهذا من زيادة التأكيد؛ لأن الواجب النقلي شأنه ذلك، ما عدا الحياة) بالجر، فما زائدة، وعدا حرف جر، فيجب على كل مكلف أن يعتقد ذلك. وحاصله: أن هذه الصفات بالنسبة للتعلق وعدمه أربعة أقسام: قسم منها لا يتعلق بشيء، وهو الحياة، إذ هي الإدراك، من غير أن تطلب أمرا زائدا على قيامها بمحلها. وقسم يتعلق، وهو ثلاثة أقسام: الأول منها: ما يتعلق بجميع أقسام الحكم العقلي، وهو صفتان: العلم والكلام، وإليه أشار بقوله: -٣٨- فالعلم جزمًا والكلام السامي * تعلقا بسائر الأقسام. ما يتعلق، وهو بدوره ثلاثة أقسام فرعية ما يتعلق بجميع أقسام الحكم العقلي، وما يتعلق بالممكنات فقط، وما يتعلق بجميع الموجودات.
And when he finished explaining the attributes of meaning (ṣifāt al-ma‘ānī), he began explaining their attachment (ta‘alluq). And attachment is: the attribute requiring an extra thing beyond its subsistence in the essence, like knowledge requiring an object known that is disclosed by it, and will requiring an object willed that is specified by it, and power requiring an object of power, and so on. So he said: (And it is intellectually obligatory) (the attachment of the possessor) i.e., these attributes (i.e., the attributes of meaning) (necessarily) i.e., perpetually, (continuously) i.e., in the manner of perpetuity and continuity, and this is from the increase of emphasis; because the obligatory by transmission (al-wājib al-naqlī) is such that, except for life) in the genitive, so 'ma' is extra and '‘adā' is a particle of genitive. So it is obligatory for every legally responsible person to believe that. Its summary: These attributes, with respect to attachment and non-attachment, are four categories: A category that does not attach to anything, which is life, for it is perception, without requiring an extra thing beyond its subsistence in its locus. And a category that attaches, and it is three categories: The first of them: that which attaches to all divisions of rational judgment (al-ḥukm al-‘aqlī), and it is two attributes: knowledge and speech, and to that he pointed with his saying: "So knowledge certainly and the lofty speech attached to all the divisions." That which attaches, and it in turn is three subcategories: that which attaches to all divisions of rational judgment, that which attaches only to possibles, and that which attaches to all existents.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification. First, the author defines 'attachment' (al-ta‘alluq) as the attribute's requirement of an extra object beyond its subsistence in the essence (e.g., knowledge requires an object known). Then he explains the verse that states it is intellectually obligatory that these attributes attach perpetually, except for life. The summary is a four-fold classification: (1) Life does not attach to anything; it is purely a condition for other attributes (like perception). (2) Knowledge and speech attach to all three rational judgments (necessary, impossible, possible). (3) Other attaching attributes are further subdivided: those that attach to all rational judgments (perhaps only knowledge and speech?), those that attach only to possibles (e.g., will), and those that attach to all existents (e.g., power). The passage concludes with the verse that begins the discussion of knowledge and speech.

Correction: Attachment means the attribute logically requires an object, not that it is physically separate.

Knowledge and Speech Attach to All Rational Judgments
Author explains that knowledge and speech attach to all three rational judgments and gives the reason.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the divine attributes of knowledge and speech necessarily relate to all three categories of rational judgment: necessary, impossible, and possible.

Core Idea
Divine knowledge and speech require an object, and that object can be any rational judgment.

In previous lessons, we learned that rational judgments are divided into three: necessary, impossible, and possible. Now Imam Dardheer clarifies a key point: the divine attributes of knowledge and speech are not limited to only some judgments; they attach to all. This passage explains why, by pointing out that both knowledge and speech require an extra object beyond themselves.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Imam Dardheer describes divine speech as lofty and free from human attributes.
2
Identify the three divisions of rational judgment
The passage lists the three divisions: necessary (wājib), impossible (mustaḥīl), and possible (jā’iz). Note that the author says knowledge and speech attach to all of them.
3
Understand the reason for attachment
Ask yourself: why must knowledge and speech attach to all three? The passage gives the answer: because each attribute requires an extra object. Knowledge requires an object known; speech requires a meaning indicated.
This connects the general rule to the specific attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العلم (فالعلم جزمًا) معمول لقوله "تعلقا" قدم عليه، (والكلام السامي) أي: العالي المرتفع القدر، المنزه عن الحروف والأصوات والتقديم والتأخير، والسكوت واللحن والإعراب، وغير ذلك مما يتصف به كلام الحوادث (تعلقا) أي: إن هاتين الصفتين تعلقا جزمًا، أي: مجزوما به بسائر (أي: بجميع جزئيات الأقسام) أي: أقسام الحكم العقلي الثلاثة، الواجب والمستحيل والجائز. أما كونهما متعلقين، فلأنها طلبا أمرًا زائدا على قيامهما بمحلهما، إذ العلم يقتضي معلوما ينكشف به، والكلام يقتضي معنى يدل عليه.
Knowledge: (for knowledge certainly) is the object of his word 'attached', preceded over it. (And the lofty speech) i.e., the high, exalted in rank, purified from letters and sounds and precedence and delay, and silence and melody (laḥn) and i‘rāb, and other than that which characterizes the speech of contingent beings. (Attached) i.e., these two attributes attached certainly, i.e., in a certain manner, to all (i.e., to all particulars of the divisions) i.e., the three divisions of rational judgment: the necessary (al-wājib), the impossible (al-mustaḥīl), and the possible (al-jā’iz). As for their being attached, it is because they require an extra thing beyond their subsistence in their locus, since knowledge requires an object known that is disclosed by it, and speech requires a meaning that it indicates.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is an explanatory commentary on the verse about knowledge and speech. It breaks down the verse phrase by phrase. 'Knowledge certainly' is the object of the verb 'attached'. 'The lofty speech' is the subject, and it describes the speech of Allah as exalted, free from letters, sounds, and all the imperfections of created speech. These two attributes attach to all three rational judgments: necessary (e.g., Allah exists), impossible (e.g., partner with Allah), and possible (e.g., creation). The reason they attach is that each requires an extra object: knowledge requires an object known, speech requires a meaning indicated.

Classification of Divine Attributes: Relating and Non-Relating
Dardeer classifies divine attributes into non-relating and relating, with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between divine attributes that require an external relation (like knowledge and speech) and those that do not (like life).

Core Idea
Life enables perception without an object; knowledge and speech require an object and a meaning.

Dardeer begins a critical classification of divine attributes based on whether they relate to something external. Life stands apart as a non-relating attribute, while knowledge and speech are relating because they demand an additional object. This distinction sharpens our understanding of how different attributes describe Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once and then its literal translation. Notice the technical terms like 'تعلق' (relate) and 'قيام' (subsistence).
2
Identify the two categories
Find where Dardeer divides attributes into 'لا يتعلق' (does not relate) and 'يتعلق' (relates). Understand that life is in the first category, and knowledge and speech in the second.
Life is described as 'إدراك' (perception) without needing anything extra.
3
Understand why knowledge and speech relate
Dardeer explains that knowledge requires an object known (معلوم) and speech requires a meaning (معنى) — both are additional to the attribute's own existence.
This relates to the broader theme of divine attributes and rational judgments.
4
Reflect on the significance
Think about why this classification matters for theology: it shows how some attributes describe Allah's essence directly, while others describe His relation to creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القسم الأول: الإلهيات. صفة تصحح لمن قامت به. قسم منها لا يتعلق بشيء، وهو الحياة، إذ هو الإدراك، من غير أن تطلب أمرًا زائدا على قيامها بمحلها. وقسم يتعلق، وهو ثلاثة أقسام: الأول منها: ما يتعلق بجميع أقسام الحكم العقلي، وهو صفتان: العلم والكلام، وإليه أشار بقوله: فالعلم جزمًا والكلام السامي * تعلقا بسائر الأقسام. أما كونها متعلقين، فلأنها طلبت أمرًا زائدا على قيامهما بمحلهما، إذ العلم يقتضي معلوما ينكشف به، والكلام يقتضي معنى يدل عليه.
The first section: Divine matters. An attribute is valid for the one in whom it subsists. A part of them does not relate to anything, and that is life, for it is perception, without requiring anything additional to its subsistence in its locus. And a part relates, and it has three divisions: the first of them is that which relates to all divisions of rational judgment, and it is two attributes: knowledge and speech. And to this he alluded in his saying: 'Knowledge certainly and lofty speech relate to all divisions.' As for their being relating, it is because they require something additional to their subsistence in their locus, since knowledge necessitates an object known that is disclosed by it, and speech necessitates a meaning that it indicates.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is a classification of divine attributes. It begins by stating that an attribute is valid for the one in whom it subsists. Then it divides attributes into two kinds: those that do not relate to anything (life) and those that relate. Life does not relate because it is merely a condition for perception without requiring any additional object. Among those that relate, there are three divisions; the first division comprises knowledge and speech, which relate to all three divisions of rational judgment (necessary, impossible, possible). The author quotes the verse from the matn (text) that says 'knowledge certainly and lofty speech relate to all divisions.' Then he explains why they are considered relating: because each requires something beyond themselves—knowledge requires an object known that becomes disclosed, and speech requires a meaning that it indicates. This shows that unlike life, they have an external relation.

The All-Encompassing Nature of Divine Knowledge
Dardeer explains how divine knowledge relates to rational judgments as disclosure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how divine knowledge relates to all rational judgments as a single eternal disclosure, distinct from speech and free from description as necessary or acquired.

Core Idea
Divine knowledge discloses everything in a single eternal act without process.

In this passage, Imam Dardeer clarifies how Allah's knowledge and speech relate to the three rational judgments. He distinguishes between knowledge as disclosure (inkishaf) and speech as indication (dalala). This lesson focuses on the unique mode of divine knowledge: it encompasses all universals and particulars, past and future, without reflection or causation, making it unlike human knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once and then the literal translation. Notice the key terms: تعلق الانكشاف and تعلق الدلالة.
The passage contrasts two modes of relation.
2
Identify the two types of relation
Dardeer mentions that knowledge relates by disclosure and speech by indication. Understand what 'disclosure' means: it uncovers the known object directly.
3
Understand the scope of divine knowledge
Knowledge relates to all universals and particulars, eternally, without reflection or deduction. How does this differ from human knowledge?
Human knowledge often requires process; divine knowledge does not.
4
Reflect on the attributes of divine knowledge
Divine knowledge is not described as 'necessary' (daruri) or 'acquired' (nazari). Why? Because those terms imply dependency or process. It has a single eternal actual relation.
This emphasizes Allah's perfection and simplicity.

Source Text

وأما تعلقهما بجميع أقسام الحكم العقلي فظاهر، إلا أن تعلقها مختلف، فتعلق العلم تعلق انكشاف، وتعلق الكلام تعلق دلالة كما فهم لما ذكرته لك. فالعلم يتعلق بجميع الكليات والجزئيات، أزلا وأبدا، بلا تأمل واستدلال، ولا سبب من الأسباب، فلا يوصف بالضروري ولا بالنظري، وله تعلق واحد تنجيزي قديم.
As for their relating to all divisions of rational judgment, it is apparent, except that their relation is different: the relation of knowledge is a relation of disclosure, and the relation of speech is a relation of indication, as understood from what I mentioned to you. For knowledge relates to all universals and particulars, eternally and forever, without reflection and deduction, and without any cause from causes, so it is not described as necessary nor as acquired, and it has a single eternal actual relation.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage explains how knowledge and speech relate to the three rational judgments. It first affirms that it is apparent that they relate to all divisions, but then points out that the mode of relation differs. Knowledge relates by disclosure (inkishaf), meaning it uncovers the known object, while speech relates by indication (dalala), meaning it points to a meaning. Knowledge encompasses all universals and particulars, past, present, and future, without needing reflection, deduction, or any cause. Therefore, divine knowledge is not described as 'necessary' (daruri) or 'acquired' (nazari) because these terms imply a process or dependency; Allah's knowledge is immediate and eternal. Finally, it states that knowledge has a single eternal actual relation—meaning its relation to all objects of knowledge is one and the same, not multiple or temporal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think divine knowledge is acquired through reasoning or is only known after creation.
Correction: Dardeer clarifies that divine knowledge is eternal, without reflection or cause, and encompasses all things from eternity.

Checkpoint
According to Dardeer, how does divine knowledge relate to its objects?
A) By indication (dalala)
B) By disclosure (inkishaf)
C) By deduction (istidlal)
D) By causation (sabab)

Key Takeaway
Divine knowledge is a single eternal disclosure that encompasses all things without process, reflection, or cause.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Knowing that Allah's knowledge of every detail of your life is a single eternal disclosure, what is one secret sin you continue to hide from others, yet you now know is fully unveiled to Him? How will you respond to this reality in the next 24 hours?
?
If Allah's knowledge encompasses all your future decisions without any process or reflection, what does that say about your perceived independence in planning your life? What is one area where you have been relying on your own reasoning rather than turning to the One who already knows the outcome?
?
Dardeer says divine knowledge is not 'necessary' nor 'acquired'—it simply is. This means Allah never has to 'figure out' anything. How does this truth confront any doubt you have about whether Allah truly understands your unique struggles? Will you trust His knowledge more than your own assessment of yourself starting today?
